  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e2e9166d-4535-457a-8e5e-d457fdb4d8a6'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer3057348130891783107"><i>Cormoran Strike is back, with his assistant Robin Ellacott, in a mystery based around soldiers returning from war.</i><br/><br/>When a mysterious package is delivered to Robin Ellacott, she is horrified to discover that it contains a woman’s severed leg.<br/><br/>Her boss, private detective Cormoran Strike, is less surprised but no less alarmed.   <span id="freeText3057348130891783107" style="display:none"><i>Cormoran Strike is back, with his assistant Robin Ellacott, in a mystery based around soldiers returning from war.</i><br /><br />When a mysterious package is delivered to Robin Ellacott, she is horrified to discover that it contains a woman’s severed leg.<br /><br />Her boss, private detective Cormoran Strike, is less surprised but no less alarmed. There are four people from his past who he thinks could be responsible – and Strike knows that any one of them is capable of sustained and unspeakable brutality.<br /><br />With the police focusing on the one suspect Strike is increasingly sure is not the perpetrator, he and Robin take matters into their own hands, and delve into the dark and twisted worlds of the other three men. But as more horrendous acts occur, time is running out for the two of them…<br /><br />Career of Evil is the third in the series featuring private detective Cormoran Strike and his assistant Robin Ellacott. A mystery and also a story of a man and a woman at a crossroads in their personal and professional lives.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3057348130891783107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">According to an interview with Val McDermid, Rowling intends to continue the series:<br/>"I really love writing these books, so I don't know that I've got <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">According to an interview with Val McDermid, Rowling intends to continue the series:<br />"I really love writing these books, so I don't know that I've got an end point in mind. One of the things I absolutely love about this genre is that, unlike Harry, where there was an overarching story, a beginning and an end, you're talking about discrete stories. So while a detective lives, you can keep giving him cases."<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_1196977033" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1196977033" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597876967p2/1343864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1196977033?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316349932" href="/book/show/25735012-career-of-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=murder-most-foul">murder-most-foul</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=class-gender-race">class-gender-race</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=mysteries">mysteries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=manly-men-and-their-manparts">manly-men-and-their-manparts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=bloody-and-gross">bloody-and-gross</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=not-quite-five-stars-but-sooo-close">not-quite-five-stars-but-sooo-close</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1196977033" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13630786158858127016"><b>June 2018</b>: This review is mostly going to be me responding to some of my own thoughts from my first review, with some extras thrown in; for example, how I was considering raising this to five stars because I loved Robert Glenister's narration so much. I love the dead tree versions of this book, but the audio adds another level. Highly recommend if you are so inclined. (I'm leaving my rating at 4.5, rounding down, for now, because of the ending. See below.)<br/><br/>Spoilery discussion of several plot poin</span>
  <span id="freeText13630786158858127016" style="display:none"><b>June 2018</b>: This review is mostly going to be me responding to some of my own thoughts from my first review, with some extras thrown in; for example, how I was considering raising this to five stars because I loved Robert Glenister's narration so much. I love the dead tree versions of this book, but the audio adds another level. Highly recommend if you are so inclined. (I'm leaving my rating at 4.5, rounding down, for now, because of the ending. See below.)<br /><br />Spoilery discussion of several plot points below. <br /><br />So firstly, having now re-read this, I can state with approximately 99% surety that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Strike firing Robin was not a ploy. He was genuinely angry with her, and unless the narrative is hiding something from us, or being deliberately misleading (which I seriously doubt), that was an action that was very much real at the time it was made. A lot of people have commented on my review over the last few years saying he only fired her to keep her safe, but no, that's not it. I think I am going to agree that the thing with selling the story to the reporter, and advertising so blatantly for Robin's replacement, THAT was a ploy. Strike had calmed down enough to think somewhat rationally by that point. He knew if he advertised their falling out, Robin would lose her appeal to the killer and he would leave her alone. Strike was taking advantage of the situation his firing of Robin created, but the initial firing itself was something that actually happened. No doubt he wants her back, and that's what the phone message Matthew deleted was all about, but we'll have to wait to find out until <i>Lethal White</i> for sure <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />I pretty much stand by the rest of my thoughts. I love Robin in this book. She and Strike make some significant errors with one another, and become terribly communicators by the end of the book. They also let their personal feelings for one another and what's going on in their lives affect all their decision making. It's just a big clusterfuck of emotions, basically. Robin doesn't want to become that useless, scared person again, and resents anyone trying to protect her, because of that. She never explains to any of them, not her mother or Matthew or Strike, just exactly why she's so adamant about remaining at work. Maybe it's too difficult for her to articulate. In addition, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she becomes extremely upset by the idea of the little girl Zahara living in the same house as the child rapist, Brockbank. She is enraged at Strike for what she sees as a refusal to help someone in dire need, someone in trouble very much as she was once in trouble. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />And Strike doesn't explain his reasons to Robin, for the most part. He's so worried about keeping her safe, he just tells her what to do and doesn't think about any of his requests will affect her. His heart is in the right place, but it's patronizing as hell. With the Zahara situation, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[there was no reason he couldn't sit Robin down and first of all listen to her and why she was so upset, and second, explain all the reasons they couldn't attempt a rescue for the girls. Instead, they all come out after the fact, after it's too late and all the damage is done, and Robin is ashamed and angry and hurt. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />And lastly, there's the ending. This is the reason I can't up this to five stars until I read <i>Lethal White</i>. What the heck is that ending even going for? It's very unclear. Is Robin going to leave Matthew at the altar? Was Strike just going to get his partner back or did he have something else in mind? (He's very clearly attracted to Robin, but knows he should keep it professional, at the same time his attraction to her definitely magnified his rage with the firing incident.) Will Robin stay married to Matthew until his thing with the message deletion and the rest of his asshattery is revealed? It's just, that smile at the end, it's so open-ended! It could just be a little happy ending tip of the hat, letting us know they will mend their relationship, or it could be more. I don't like the ambiguity. So, 4.5 stars it remains.<br /><br /><i>Lethal White</i> is in the can, so here's hoping for a late 2018 release date. I need some answers.<br /><br /><b>October 2015</b>: Oh, man, I have so many thoughts. And I'm also not entirely sure what I think about some of what happened in this book. On the one hand, I LOVED IT. The case and Robin and Strike's personal lives dovetailed beautifully. So much of this book was character shiz, which is my favorite kind of shiz. And I've been saying for the past two books that I wanted MORE ROBIN and MORE ROBIN is exactly what I got. Robin backstory. Robin frontstory. Robin Robin Robin. <br /><br />And the mystery itself was good and different from the last two. In the first book, it was really procedural. Lots of interviews, pounding the pavement, and the central question of whether or not Lula Landry killed herself. It was also an examination of fame and the press. The second book started off as a simple missing persons case that turned into a murder mystery, but it was really a satirization of the publishing industry. But to really make it the trifecta of things JKR is obsessed with, likely because of her own fame in the publishing industry as a woman, this book and its central mystery are all about misogyny and violence against women. The book opens with Robin being sent a woman's severed leg in the mail, and it doesn't let up from there.<br /><br />This case is personal for both Strike and Robin. Strike, because the leg was sent to Robin, the killer is targeting Robin, to get at Strike. There are three men from Strike's past who would be violent and unhinged enough to do something like this. And Robin because of her own history. We finally learn why she dropped out of University. I know that some people have had (and will have) trouble with Robin's backstory, but I don't. Firstly, because it doesn't feel cheap. It feels earned. JKR has clearly been setting it up since day one. And secondly because of Robin herself. Beautiful, complicated, strong and vulnerable Robin. Certainly what happened to her was terrible and traumatizing, but it's not the event itself she has trouble with, but how her friends and family (and Strike) treat her and her ambitions afterwards that she has the most trouble with. <br /><br />Which brings me to Matthew. Motherfucking Matthew. He's just terrible. But this book sheds light on why Robin is with him, despite his terribleness. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Robin, raped and left for dead by her attacker, left that experience with her ability to empathize amplified, but her ambitions pushed aside by her own trauma, and her family constantly wanting to protect her. She spends years recovering, taking self-defense classes, learning defensive driving, and she's finally reached a place in her life where she is starting to want to move beyond the safe and easy place in her life that Matthew represents. She starts chafing against his insecurity, his disrespect for her, and his inability to see her as the person she feels she is, rather than the one he wants her to be. When she broke up with him half-way through, I was so relieved. Robin herself was so sad at losing that part of her life, but I felt she would eventually come out the other side stronger. I suppose that's still possible, but I think the way it actually shakes out, with her giving in and taking him back after he shows what she sees as true remorse, is the more plausible option. I don't think someone in Robin's mindset, so generous in her feelings for other people, so loyal to someone who's been a huge part of her life for nine years, would be able to just cut ties immediately. I think it's going to be a long, hard process for her. <br /><br />I did feel badly for Matthew in the same instance Robin did, even though I still thought he was a shithead, but he completely lost any and all goodwill the moment he listened to Strike's message for Robin and then deleted it. That is completely and utterly awful, almost worse than him cheating on her during her convalescence, because it means he has no regard for her or her own choices at all. And now she's MARRIED to the fucker! I do hope that Robin's bright smile at Strike at the end means that we won't have to put up with him for long, and that Robin can finally escape out from the shadow of her own fear and misplaced compassion long enough to be happy. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The stress of the case also works on Strike and Robin's relationship, and a large portion of the book is spent on <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the dissolution of their partnership, and the crumbling of their business <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, just as the killer intended (although I don't think he's smart enough to have foreseen the psychological nuances of the situation he created--he was going for the blunt force option, framing Strike for murder and taking something away from him, not knowing that the more subtle approach was almost as hurtful). The depth of their conflict and interpersonal relationships is what makes this book so great. <br /><br />The two things I do feel conflicted about were: <br /><br />1) The decision to have POV chapters from the killer. I'm not sure those were entirely successful. Maybe I'm just not bad enough, but they seemed overly evil to me? I don't know. They didn't work as well for me as I wanted them to. The villain himself when seen from Robin and Strike's POV was great, and I liked the way his POVs kept leading me in opposite directions. I was CONVINCED that one guy had done it, but then it turned out to be something totally unexpected, but obvious in retrospect. It's just, those POVs were so . . . blunt? They served their purpose, though.<br /><br />and 2) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Strike getting angry enough to fire Robin totally took me by surprise, but in a bad way. It felt off. Maybe I was just expecting the story to go in a different direction and missed all the clues, but I kept thinking it would all be a trick, that Strike wouldn't do that, wouldn't get that angry. It didn't seem explained enough. I feel like I need to go back and re-read the whole thing to look for the clues along the way. The only thing I can think is that he was also in the middle of falling in love with her, and was upset already that she had taken Matthew back, and her resentment at being sidelined as he tried to protect her had driven them apart, so it was just a huge mess of angry feelings that all came out in that moment, and he fired her. Or maybe there was something in that deleted message (fucking Matthew) that explains it. I guess I'll have to wait for the next book. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I think I'm going to have to just wait for the next book, and hope for the best. For now, this gets 4.5 stars. And hopefully by this time next year we'll have book four.<br /><br />[4.5 stars]<br /><br /><b>February 2015</b>: A girl could get spoiled with a new JK Rowling book every year, I tell you what.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13630786158858127016" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1197590458" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1197590458" />
    <a title="Mohammed Arabey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13592557-mohammed-arabey"><img alt="Mohammed Arabey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364338486p2/13592557.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1197590458?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mohammed Arabey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mohammed Arabey" href="/user/show/13592557-mohammed-arabey">Mohammed Arabey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

  <span id="freeText17746185110141461028" style="display:none">It's <b>The One With All the Feelings..<br>A tense,thrill mystery interwoven with complicated emotions, kind of love..even Nostalgia.</b><br>No matter how you imaged <b>Strike</b>, <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447244236i/16976127._SY540_.jpg" width="430" height="477" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480475068i/21314407._SX540_.jpg" width="430" height="241" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Here you'll get more into him, into his <b>Feelings</b> specially toward his precious engaged partner, <b>Robin</b>..his friends,<i>-I bet you gonna Love <b>Shanker</b>-</i>..<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447156234i/16964341._SY540_.png" width="220" height="297" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447156234i/16964342.png" width="209" height="297" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>ِ..into his past, During his..<b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434033532i/15169645.png" width="430" height="447" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>..Career of Evil.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447085502ra/16954386.gif" width="400" height="172" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></b><br>&amp; No matter whether you read the previous ones or not, you'll adore the Remarkable, excellent written, relation of Strike &amp; Robin..<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446297420i/16784783.jpg" width="430" height="387" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480475811i/21314479._SX540_.jpg" width="430" height="241" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b><br>This wonderful unique chemistry between them.. part admiration, part comfortable, exceptional partnership and a little bit of un-name-able kind of can-be love.<br>It has started 3 years ago -one year in the story timeline-,since she came to 12 Bar Cafe as an unwanted temp.<br></b><i><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/667280776" rel="nofollow noopener">lf you read the first book</a> that what will make you really nostalgic when you read this one..with all the characters and events developments. </i><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423666714i/13656145.png" width="323" height="250" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>And this time their relation facing a really hard time, some maniac blood and body parts craving murderer is set to sabotage Strike's career and reputation, and then..finish him.<br>and this murderer made clear that he's targeting Robin as a main mean to do so.<br> And not to mention the approaching of Robin's Wedding date to her Strike's hater fiancée, Matthew..and a huge fight that may stop the wedding that will increase the complications. <br><br> Because hard times make people more vulnerable emotionally, and relations usually get deeper. And this case made Strike and Robin face the darkest, hardest time..all that made this book the one with all the mixed feelings and emotions that very great written , as Rowling's best story telling usual..<br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447085502i/16954387.png" width="297" height="456" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>And it's not only the feelings of Strike and Robin, You'll get more into Robin's personal life in this one since she have bigger part, and not only her... it has larger scale of Feelings..<br> <br>The feeling of the amputees , and a strange mental disorder that made some healthy wanna be so. -first time to hear about this community-<br><b><br>The Feelings of women who unfortunately end up with the wrong guy, whether they still staying ,suffering, with them...or who from their past and left them broken and lonely..<br>Some of them may be just boyfriend, a stepfather, a husband, even a brother..or may be a fiancée that his girl not knowing how wrong her choice is...<br><br> And most importantly in the main story, The feeling of women and even little girls who suffered sexual abuses, from strangers or even someone close... how that change their lives ,the feeling of unsecured and shuttered.how sometimes the police make it hard time for the women while taking their statements.<br><br>It's really big story this time, and told you, full of feelings..<br><br>The Story<br>-------<br>A very perfect constructed Story , with faster than the first 'Cuckoo's Calling' and larger in the main characters' life and emotions..friends and family And adversaries..<br></b><br>Robin -instead of Wedding party cameras- received a served woman's leg addressed to her in Cormoran's office.<br>It's seem to be someone want to bring Cormoran Strike's businesses down and he made a satisfying success..<br><br>Strike could think of 4, or 3 main suspect capable of doing so, they're from his past..and one of them is his late 'stepfather' who Strike already suspect he has murdered his mother..<br><br>And that's not all..now this bloody murderer not only want vengeance of Strike, but also made it clear that he's targeting what seems to him Strike's weakness...Robin.<br><br>Why this murderer need vengeance will lead Strike to think more into his past, his<b> career</b> being in the Special Investigations Branch..<br>also will lead him into more thinking of Robin, who endanger her life keeping her work with him.. also thinking of her fast approaching Wedding to Matthew, who may take her off his life..<br>The life of a lone wolf..<br><b>The Lone Wolf<br>~~~~~~~~~~~~</b><i>
  <blockquote>Yet he knew he had been left impaired, that he no longer had the capacity to feel in the way that he had once felt. Elin’s distress of the previous evening had not touched him at his core in the way Charlotte’s had once done. He felt as though his capacity for loving had been blunted, the nerve endings severed. <br>He had not intended to wound Elin; he did not enjoy seeing her cry; yet the ability to feel empathetic pain seemed to have closed down. A small part of him, in truth, had been mentally planning his route home as she sobbed.</blockquote>
</i><b><br>No doubt whoever well read the stories of Cormoran Strike will really feel how deep and interesting character he is..<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423670270i/13656574.png" width="400" height="513" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></b><br><i>I always imaged him as Hugh Jackman, but since that I had a big backlash comments about him I changed the main photo to -BASED ON FRIENDS and GOODREADS USERS COMMENTS that mentioned other actors both on my Silkworm and this novel's pre review, I choose the most accurate ones..<br>Also Thank you <a href="https://schmidtjohnson.wordpress.com/2015/10/30/career-of-evil-cormoran-strike/" rel="nofollow noopener">Steph</a> for the mention in your blog, and the idea of the particular scene of X-Men I used for Strike portrait.</i><br> <br>It was great How Mr. Robert Galbraith described the deep feelings for a lone wolf, who had a broken heart before , not that social, haunted by his past and infamous life of his mother..and has this complicated relation with his businesses partner 'Robin'..<br>you can clearly see how he defend himself of admitting he truly loves her without writing direct lines, you will observe that through his actions with Robin.<br><br>Strike is really interesting character, and so is Robin..so is all the characters that been mentioned before but get bigger role this time..<br> And it's why I really don't care much about the not-related-to-the-case stuff that the books usually full with.<b><br>And here you'll get into more of them, their past..family and friends..and even adversaries..<br><br>The Career of Evil<br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br>Tensed fast thrilled that full of emotions and feelings and many horrible bloody scenes.<br>This time full of real tense and some chapters ends in a real cliffhangers. <br></b>-I am writing this review by the last 15% of the novel, with a cliffhanger dangers the continuation of Robin in the next stories.-<br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447085502i/16954388.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>The novel is obsessed with the many references<b> Blue Oyster Cult</b>, which is have a base in the core of the novel's mystery since the murderer seems obsessed with this band as well.<br>You can see the phrases of their songs' lyrics in every chapter..<br><br>And, as the rest of the series, it's like a detailed <b>Travel literature</b> into England..you visit many places, interesting ones..<br>such as -for example here-:<br>Barrow-in-Furness and it's gloomy streets and nuclear submarines bunkers. <br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446595298i/16839468._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="266" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The interesting Market Harborough<br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446595298i/16839467._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="266" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The Sweet entrance of Catford Shopping Centre<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447086282i/16954467._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="375" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And many many more..<br><br>And also living the atmosphere of the time the novel taking place, here in the April-June 2011, the major thing in GB was the Royal Wedding..<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447160890i/16964624._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="225" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And, this time, interweaving all these places and events with the main core of the story is more than marvellous.<br>-As the Royal Wedding and Robin Story for example-<br><b><br><s> J.K. Rowling</s> Robert Galbraith<br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382098796i/5663586.jpg" width="391" height="314" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></b><br>I guess one of the advantages of using a man , an Ex-SIB officer and actually a man, is being free to do all these bloody scenes some of it Stephen King's bloody type.<i>
  <blockquote>
<br>Women were so petty, mean, dirty and small. Sulky bitches, the lot of them, expecting men to keep them happy. Only when they lay dead and empty in front of you did they become purified, mysterious and even wonderful. They were entirely yours then, unable to argue or struggle or leave, yours to do with whatever you liked.</blockquote>
</i><br>As well the great description of the murderer mind, it was also super insight into the feelings of women who suffered rape or sexual abuses..it was very realistic and even the reaction of the ones near the sufferer or the toughness of some police officers is very well stated in the novel.<br><br>SO, it's still her, the Queen of Magic, master storytelling elements, getting deep into characters and their feeling, analysing body language and actions without waiting for explanations..<br><b>Humorous moments and deep meaning ones, that's what you will fall in love with this series because of this unique storytelling style.</b><i>
  <blockquote>“You could find beauty nearly anywhere if you stopped to look for it, but the battle to get through the days made it easy to forget that this totally cost-free luxury existed.”</blockquote>
</i><b><br>That's , of course, if you don't mind many, or much, digressions.<br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447086282i/16954468._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="244" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></b><br>Now I must go to read the last 75 pages to see what will happen to Robin...and who the bloody murderer will be...<br><i>-The Review of 9 Nov. 2015 ends here</i><b><br><br>Let's Talk the Ending..<br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br></b><i>AGAIN</i>ِ, <b>It's The One With All the Feelings...<br>The One with All the Emotions..<br>The One with All the Tense..<br>And all the tensed bloody thrill and slowly resolving the hard, very well constructed mystery in a thrilling double climax..<br><br>Then came the very Bittersweet Ending..</b><br>Without giving much , as a dear friend has said "Bloody Hell" or as Robin says "Bugger" <br>An Ending that will leave you grinning, sad a bit, feeling you wanna know more, you wanna more pages ,you don't want to leave them..<br>The ending...so tense..more excited I was really on the edge of my seat ,literally holding my breath..<br><br>Oh God the Ending...<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[..Oh The Wedding, I kept wishing -with Friends' Season Three finale in mind , which was also in England :)-..."Please Say Take The Strike :)<br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447201848ra/16969233.gif" width="400" height="178" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> not take the Matthew ...<br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447201848ra/16969234.gif" width="400" height="207" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But what really pissed me off was the report not mentioning Strike at the first news after catching the killer ,that really made me very ferious ..I guess though they will when the trials starts ,right?<br>If not I'll come to the Mets and kick some arse..<br><br>AND Matthew , man ,what an ass blocking Strike by the end.. now I really hate him so much..<br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br>these 2 last points about the ending really pissed me off, but not with the novel of course...it is really one of my best reads<br><br><b>How to know you've been reading a real good,even brilliant literature..<br></b>well, I had the symptoms of loss by finishing the novel, after about 12 days of reading as slowly as possible to not end it.....<br>1-I was really deep thinking ,kinda haunted with the story and keeping the details in mind..,how long did it pass since we 'Strike,Robin and me' received the leg..and who will be the real murderer of the three suspects..<br><br>2- The waiter in the cafe I read at told me today "you've been in this book, for few days you've been tensed sometimes and widely grinning many times" , hell yeah I did :) ... I caught myself grinning a lot despite controlling so while I'm in public cafe, siting alone..<br><br>3- I Don't know what can I read next although I had a plan for 3 big horrors.I can't see myself committing with big novels now, may be even any novel for a day or two...<b> I just wanna read the next Strike's novel..<br><br>So Please Mr.Galbraith.. do your best , I know you always do..:)<br></b><br>Mohammed Arabey<br>From 27 Oct. 2015<br>To 10 Nov. 2015<br><br>First pre- review in the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><b>..After the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/667280776" rel="nofollow noopener">infamous side of celebrities' life</a><br>and the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/754737354" rel="nofollow noopener">horrible side of writers and publishers' life</a>..<br><blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423666714i/13656145.png" width="323" height="250" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></blockquote>
<br>This time Will be <u>"Career of Evil"</u><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434033532i/15169645.png" width="400" height="437" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Will be about the experience of returning soldiers..with story seems darker..and more complicated with Robin too..<br><a href="http://www.theguardian.com/books/2015/oct/09/career-of-evil-robert-galbraith-jk-rowling-cormoran-strike-first-chapter-extract" rel="nofollow noopener">BLOODY Chapter One</a><br><a href="http://time.com/4067478/robert-galbraith-jk-rowling/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Surprising Chapter Two</a><br>Can't wait again to meet Mr. Strike again,<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423670270i/13656574.png" width="400" height="513" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And our sweetheart .. Robin<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436133664i/15422615._SY540_.png" width="400" height="560" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></b><br>Oh Please if anyone can convince Mr. Hugh Jackman ,he'd be Perfect Cormoran Strike ,isn't he?<br>And for sorry it will be out by autumn..<br>And it will be more than 7 Books, I guess you already know that :)<br><br>AND PLZ STOP RATING, STOP HIGH AND LOW RATINGS.<br><br>Mohammed Arabey<br>11 Feb. 2015<br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1308862583" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1308862583" />
    <a title="Alejandro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro"><img alt="Alejandro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328672389p2/665584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1308862583?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alejandro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alejandro" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro">Alejandro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316349932" href="/book/show/25735012-career-of-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=military">military</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=detective">detective</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1308862583" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8996356694687316293"><b>
  <u>Sadly, I felt it as a recoil in the book series.</u>
</b><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>BACKGROUND</u>
</b><br/><br/>I was quite excited to read this third novel in the <i>Cormoran Strike</i> book series, since I had enjoyed plenty enough, however I think that this third novel was like a retrogression in what the book series was able to accomplish and to develop so far.<br/><br/><i>The Cuckoo’s Calling</i> was slow pacing, drifting to irrelevant sub-plots, over detailed filling scenes and repetitive situations, along with having more pages than necessary, <b>BUT</b> I was ada</span>
  <span id="freeText8996356694687316293" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Sadly, I felt it as a recoil in the book series.</u>
</b><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>BACKGROUND</u>
</b><br /><br />I was quite excited to read this third novel in the <i>Cormoran Strike</i> book series, since I had enjoyed plenty enough, however I think that this third novel was like a retrogression in what the book series was able to accomplish and to develop so far.<br /><br /><i>The Cuckoo’s Calling</i> was slow pacing, drifting to irrelevant sub-plots, over detailed filling scenes and repetitive situations, along with having more pages than necessary, <b>BUT</b> I was adamant to any reader of my review that they should keep at it since the climax was superb and making worthy all the effort to read the novel, also the use of the fashion/modeling industry was a real plus.<br /><br /><i>The Silkworm</i> became a fresh air to the rising book series, since it was like magic (yep, pun intended!) due that all those negative elements in the first book were gone. The second novel was intense, focused on the case, each scene was different, even the book was thinner, adding the use of the book publishing industry, easily this book turned to be the best in the series (clearly having in mind that there were only two in the series, so far) but also a “must-read” to any J.K. Rowling fan (yes, it’s her, just in case you are the last one to know that “Robert Galbraith” is just a pseudonym), since I felt it as a very personal book by her, showing light to many feelings from her about the craziness amd intrigue involved in the industry of publishing books. Moreover, since there weren’t any spoilers about the first case, you could easily engage this second novel (without having read the first book) and you wouldn’t be any lost in the reading.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>LIKE A CRAB</u>
</b><br /><br /><i>Career of Evil</i> fell in all the mistakes found the first book and even worse, since this time you don’t have a specific industry involved in the story (I thought earlier that it would be about the music industry that it could be real cool, but no), also it’s not a case per se, since there isn’t anybody who hired Cormoran, but it’s a personal vendetta by some mysterious person but clearly someone from Cormoran’s past, which made quite dumb that he needed so much time to deduce the culprit since he knew quite well all the suspects, and where Cormoran looked as a brilliant detective in how he cracked the previous two cases and how the climaxes were developed, however here (I won’t make any spoilers, don’t worry), let’s just say that his key evidence is something so trivial, so small, along with a non-climatic resolve, that after reading almost 500 pages I felt cheated.<br /><br />Realizing that it’s a book by J.K. Rowling, which is the alive female writer that I respected the most, it just made more disappointing the whole reading experience of this third book in the series.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE GOOD SIDE</u>
</b><br /><br />Commenting about the good side in the book... mmh... well, there is... mmh... aah!... mmh... no... wait!... mmh... nope... Really, I can’t say anything good about the third book.<br /><br />Still, I guess that some basic expected elements in the construction of a book, by such accomplished writer, helped to get at least two stars for my personal rating.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8996356694687316293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1289327858" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1289327858" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2431873-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1477433724p2/2431873.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1289327858?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/2431873-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780751562279" href="/book/show/24106033-career-of-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2431873-emily?shelf=detective-series">detective-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2431873-emily?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1289327858" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer977315329325906763">If the first two Cormoran Strike books can be summed up as "celebrity" and "publishing" respectively, then this book is "misogynistic violence," which is possibly my least favorite subject to read about. <br/><br/>This is a closed circle mystery in which Robin and Strike investigate a serial killer whose past is linked to Strike. Due to the fact that there are only four real suspects that are provided by Strike - and that the killer gets his own POV sections in which you see some of the murders happen - t</span>
  <span id="freeText977315329325906763" style="display:none">If the first two Cormoran Strike books can be summed up as "celebrity" and "publishing" respectively, then this book is "misogynistic violence," which is possibly my least favorite subject to read about. <br /><br />This is a closed circle mystery in which Robin and Strike investigate a serial killer whose past is linked to Strike. Due to the fact that there are only four real suspects that are provided by Strike - and that the killer gets his own POV sections in which you see some of the murders happen - this mystery isn't particularly interesting or fun to solve. The Strike/Robin relationship is further developed in this book, which is good because otherwise this would have been 400 pages of stakeouts interspersed with scenes of horrific assaults. In short, it's boring. J.K. Rowling can still propel me through a story, but I'm amazed that this particular story took so many pages to tell.<br /><br />As a disclaimer before I keep writing: I understand that sexual violence is an extremely important topic to continue discussing openly, both to remove stigmatization of victims and because it's so prevalent: <a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2011/12/15/health/nearly-1-in-5-women-in-us-survey-report-sexual-assault.html?_r=0" rel="nofollow noopener">1 in 5 American women will be sexually assaulted in their lifetimes</a>. But I personally do not enjoy reading graphic depictions of sexual violence. (I'd rather read the discovery of the body of Owen Quine several times than read some of the descriptions in this book again.) And it's always hard to tell if its inclusion is titillating or not. If I didn't already trust J.K. Rowling as a writer, I probably would have abandoned this book near the halfway point. <br /><br />My least favorite part about this book was the use of rape as a backstory. When a female character needs a life-altering turning point in her past that explains her decisions and current trajectory, rape gets slotted in as the most traumatic event possible. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It really, really bothered me that Robin was saddled with this backstory. On one hand, yes, this is a book about the prevalence of violent assault, but on the other hand, this gives a weird tinge to Robin's desire to become a detective. Rowling takes care to explicitly say that Robin wanted to be an investigator before the rape, but I wholeheartedly wish that that wasn't even in the mix. <br /><br />This also bothered me because it felt like a cheap way to explain why Robin and Matthew are still together. Relationships are complicated and messy. They don't always make logical sense to an external viewer, and they sometimes don't even make sense to the people in them. The rape backstory reduces Robin and Matthew to a comfort-level relationship where Robin holds on to him only because of her past. In a way, it would be more interesting for inertia to play a bigger role, without the linchpin of Robin's trauma. Matthew gets written as an even bigger asshole (excuse me, "wanker") in this book, which felt like an excuse for the Robin/Strike relationship to develop rather than a true picture of the nine-year Robin/Matthew relationship. <br /><br />It's even harder to understand why Robin and Matthew get back together, outside of that inertia and nine years, when you don't see any of the good parts that must exist. And the fact that the book ends on Robin's "I do" felt cheap. On one hand, yes, the Robin/Strike relationship is what keeps me going through these books. On the other hand, are these mystery novels or not? Shouldn't the mysteries be good enough that I don't have to be distracted overly by the other drama? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />There is exploration of victimhood here, and what it means to be a victim. It comes up again when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Robin is compelled to go to Alyssa to get her children away from Brockbank. Strike doesn't know what it's like to be small and powerless, and Robin does, and that's why she goes <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. And when Strike goes to see Hazel Furley, he thinks to himself that it's natural that the cops should have questioned her boyfriend Ray so intensely: "most women's rapists and killers were not strangers in masks who reached out of the dark space under the stairs. They were the father, the husband, the mother's or the sister's boyfriend ..." <br /><br />But I believe that exploration is undercut by the frequent and extremely graphic scenes of rape, dismemberment, and assault. It's one thing to recognize the horror that these acts recur too frequently in the world, and to explore how resilience can play a part in moving on and not letting that experience define you. It's another to have a mother (Rhona Laing's mother, to be exact) explain that one of the suspects <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[raped her daughter with a knife and permanently prevented her from having children <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> - and that's not even close to the first-person scenes from the murderer's perspective, where he talks about women as objects who are better to him dead before killing them. <br /><br />Does every book that involves sexual assault have to have an underlying moral or point? No, of course not. But if I am expected as the reader to make my way through these various scenes, there should be some sort of payoff. Given that this mystery is not interesting, novel, or fun to read, this book completely failed for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="977315329325906763" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1693720946" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1693720946" />
    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<div id="review_1373225117" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1373225117" />
    <a title="Alex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12291273-alex"><img alt="Alex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1449450142p2/12291273.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1373225117?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/12291273-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780751562279" href="/book/show/24106033-career-of-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1373225117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3122037153986441230">Jesus, what a rollercoaster! I have been looking forward to this book for such a long time with a mixture of anticipation and trepidation. What if this wasn't as good as the other two in the series? What if I had somehow built up the other two books in retrospect, leaving only disappointment in the third? Would I ever stop with the rhetorical questions and get on with the review? <br/><br/>Let me tell you: this was fucking good. Like REALLY GODDAMNED GOOD. Like I-stayed-up-way-past-my-bedtime-to-finish-th</span>
  <span id="freeText3122037153986441230" style="display:none">Jesus, what a rollercoaster! I have been looking forward to this book for such a long time with a mixture of anticipation and trepidation. What if this wasn't as good as the other two in the series? What if I had somehow built up the other two books in retrospect, leaving only disappointment in the third? Would I ever stop with the rhetorical questions and get on with the review? <br /><br />Let me tell you: this was fucking good. Like REALLY GODDAMNED GOOD. Like I-stayed-up-way-past-my-bedtime-to-finish-this good. The book starts off at a sprint and just keeps going, and I think this is my favourite out of all three of Robert Galbraith's books. There's something about the murder mystery in this book that I really, REALLY enjoyed. It wasn't as heavy with exposition as The Cuckoo's Calling (anyone else remember the paragraphs of dialogue from that book?), nor as outlandish as The Silkworm. This serial killer was creepy, realistic, sadistic, and the question of who he actually turns out to be is set up so well that I couldn't figure it out until the last third or so.<br /><br />Speaking of the last third - OH MY GOD. SHIT GOES DOWN. I realise this isn't my most coherent review but I'm currently coming down from my Career of Evil-induced high. I was alternately laughing like a maniac, screaming at a book and jumping up and down in excitement. People thought I was possessed. Note to self: don't scream with all the windows open or the neighbours will think you're weird. <br /><br />In terms of characters, Cormoran is back being his usual awesome self, and there are some great new characters introduced in this book (hi, Shanker!), but the real badass is Robin. I love her. She is so fucking awesome that I can hardly form coherent sentences. What a badass. What. A. Bad. Ass. She is the heart, soul, and central nervous system of these books, which took me a while to figure out, but now that I realise this I love and admire her as a character even more. She goes from strength to strength and I cannot wait to see how she develops in future books. I'm officially crushing majorly on her. WHAT A BADASS.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I should also mention that Robin and Cormoran are my new favourite OTP. I had my doubts that an eventual pairing was the direction they were headed in the first book, but my opinion is now cemented. CHAPTER 40 is all I will say on that front. As someone who reviewed this book in a newspaper said, their cautious non-courtship is so entertaining.<br /><br />On the subject of relationships, WHAT THE FUCK ARE YOU THINKING, ROBIN? Matthew is the limpest of limp dishrags. I had a moment's sympathy for him, rapidly drowned out by the realisation that he's still a vain, smug, overbearing, disrespectful dickwad who does not deserve you.<br /><br />Finally - no more Cormoran mooning over Charlotte here. Thank god. That bitch is crazy and I am kind of hoping she turns up as either the victim or the suspect in a subsequent book <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />If you liked the other Cormoran Strike books, you will like this, or at least I assume you will. I loved it. I haven't had a book keep me up all night in a while, and this did that and more. It had my heart racing. It made my neighbours think I am some sort of super excitable psychopath who screams at poor inanimate books. And it reaffirmed my love for Robin, who is as great a female character in any book I've ever read.<br /><br /><br />*** UPDATE ***<br /><br />Ok so I've had a few more days to think about this book, and there is one thing in particular that I really need to get off my chest. My family hasn't read this book yet, so I'm forced to unleash my feelings upon my fellow Goodreaders.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[MATTHEW CUNLIFFE. I read the book, had some sympathy in some parts and had significantly less sympathy in others, but now that I'm a few days out of my reading experience, I have Definite Feelings(TM) about Matt.<br /><br />WHAT. A. DICK. What a two-faced prick, meddling with Robin's mobile and her interactions with Strike. She has NEVER given him any plausible reason to think that she can't be trusted - as anyone who has read <i>Career of Evil</i> knows, Matt is the one who has been untrustworthy in more ways than one, from his cheating on Robin during the worst moment of her life to him gleefully presenting her with the newspaper showing that Cormoran is already advertising for a replacement for her.<br /><br />I was just thinking about this, and I was dumbstruck firstly by what a raging asshole Matt is, and secondly that Robin has no perceivable notion of what her fiancée is really like. I think it's the invasion of privacy that is REALLY ticking me off - if the revelation of him cheating can't break the relationship, surely the knowledge that her fiancée (now husband - regrettably) not only doesn't trust her but is actively working against her to keep her from her ambitions must. As Shanker says, Robin is kind and good, and really doesn't deserve to be dragged down by such a dead weight. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Ah I had to get that off my chest. It's all I've been thinking about since I finished the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3122037153986441230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1959158427" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1959158427" />
    <a title="Adina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22189348-adina"><img alt="Adina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531917330p2/22189348.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1959158427?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adina" href="/user/show/22189348-adina">Adina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316349932" href="/book/show/25735012-career-of-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22189348-adina?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22189348-adina?shelf=british">british</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1959158427" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2107316321094056726">Wow, I can’t believe it’s been 2 weeks since my last review. I had two hectic weeks at work and home and had no time to read and even less to review. I hope to be able to catch up with my challenge and reviews in the following days.<br/><br/>Career of Evil is the third volume in Cormoran Strike series and in case you did not know, written by wonderful J.K. Rowling under the pen name of Robert Galbraith. If you haven’t read the other two books do not start with this one. They are to be read in order as the</span>
  <span id="freeText2107316321094056726" style="display:none">Wow, I can’t believe it’s been 2 weeks since my last review. I had two hectic weeks at work and home and had no time to read and even less to review. I hope to be able to catch up with my challenge and reviews in the following days.<br /><br />Career of Evil is the third volume in Cormoran Strike series and in case you did not know, written by wonderful J.K. Rowling under the pen name of Robert Galbraith. If you haven’t read the other two books do not start with this one. They are to be read in order as the personal life of the characters is mingled with the murder mystery. <br /><br />I am not going to write anything about the story as the blurb is pretty well done. I am just going to make some comparisons with the other two and talk about what I liked and what I did not. <br /><br />What I love about is series are the two characters, Robin and Cormoran, and the dynamic of their relationship. They are both complex and this volume is the one where we get to learn more about their past which was ta part I was looking forward to explore. However, there was a bit too much drama between the two of them and it took a bit away from my satisfaction. <br /><br />There is a big difference between Career of Evil and the first two books, namely, the duo is chasing a serial killer this time. I prefer mysteries where the killers have complex reasons for acting violently and serial murders are not fully my type. Nevertheless, I enjoyed reading the small chapters where we were given a glimpse inside the madman’s mind. The pace was a bit slower than in the other novels and the focus was made on surveillance rather then on discussions with potential suspects which I found less interesting. <br /><br />Although it was my least favorite of the Strike’s adventures, I still enjoyed every page and I can’t wait to read the next one. Hurry up, J.K, please. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2107316321094056726" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1399196969" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1399196969" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1399196969?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316349932" href="/book/show/25735012-career-of-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1399196969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14391951910025125742">Once again, left with post-novel depression as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/383606.Robert_Galbraith' title='Robert Galbraith' rel='nofollow noopener'>Robert Galbraith</a> has published another well-written Strike/Ellacott novel. Boy was this a wild ride! I have felt each book in this series has grabbed my attention more than the previous one and leaves me craving another. <br/><br/>Set in 2011 (one year after Robin has begun working for Cormoran Strike and during the time of the royal wedding), the story opens with the ramblings of a serial killer who's identity is a mystery to the reader. Robin Ellacott has b</span>
  <span id="freeText14391951910025125742" style="display:none">Once again, left with post-novel depression as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/383606.Robert_Galbraith" title="Robert Galbraith" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Galbraith</a> has published another well-written Strike/Ellacott novel. Boy was this a wild ride! I have felt each book in this series has grabbed my attention more than the previous one and leaves me craving another. <br /><br />Set in 2011 (one year after Robin has begun working for Cormoran Strike and during the time of the royal wedding), the story opens with the ramblings of a serial killer who's identity is a mystery to the reader. Robin Ellacott has been sent a female severed leg in the mail and the dynamic duo decide to hunt down this killer while the police are heading in what Strike considers a dead end. Cormoran has 3 suspects in mind and they spend the entirety of the book bouncing back and forth all 3 while keeping us in suspense until the very last pages. Simultaneously, Robin and Strike's relationship takes a new turn as Robin and her fiancé take a break to decide if the wedding will take place at all. <br /><br />I loved how the author really developed Strike and Robin's relationship deeper than both the previous novels together. I was just as engrossed in this aspect as I was in the suspense of the killer. There was a really nice twist at the end involving the identity of the killer which I did not see coming; honestly, she does a great job of keeping you from knowing who the killer is entirely until she wants it revealed. I really enjoyed how the chapters were structured by breaking up the story chapters with sections of the killer's private thoughts. This is by far one of my favorite books of the year and I am anxiously awaiting the fourth novel in the series!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14391951910025125742" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1643532678" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1643532678" />
    <a title="Paromjit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit"><img alt="Paromjit" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1643532678?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paromjit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paromjit" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit">Paromjit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316349932" href="/book/show/25735012-career-of-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1643532678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13737653871546170246">This is an intense, atmospheric and compelling addition to the Cormoran Strike series. Where it really excels is in characterisation with in depth backstories of Cormoran and his history with the three main suspects in this story and his relationship with Shanker, his offbeat and eccentric friend. Robin's traumatic history is revealed, as is the reason why working as a PI is so heartbreakingly important to her. She comes across as emotionally fragile, compassionate, tenacious and highly skilled </span>
  <span id="freeText13737653871546170246" style="display:none">This is an intense, atmospheric and compelling addition to the Cormoran Strike series. Where it really excels is in characterisation with in depth backstories of Cormoran and his history with the three main suspects in this story and his relationship with Shanker, his offbeat and eccentric friend. Robin's traumatic history is revealed, as is the reason why working as a PI is so heartbreakingly important to her. She comes across as emotionally fragile, compassionate, tenacious and highly skilled as a investigator. As for the three main suspects in the story, I think the author stood in front of the mirror, asking Who is the foulest of them all? I can see her having great fun creating the depraved, brutal, and ruthless monsters that are Whittaker, Laing and Brockbank. Those three are truly scraping the bottom of the barrel of human scum. In a well constructed story, we encounter the extreme mental health issues of people who would voluntarily amputate body parts, seek paralysis etc..<br /><br />It all begins with Robin receiving a girl's leg in a parcel. This has significance for Cormoran and he identifies 4 suspects. The police focus on who Cormoran feels is the least likely suspect, so he and Robin investigate the others. There are references to Blue Oyster Cult songs and lyrics throughout which are connected to Strike's dead mother, Leda. The investigation takes Cormoran and Robin all round the country as more murders take place on what is a dangerous trail. It becomes abundantly clear that a clever and twisted killer wants to destroy Cormoran and killing Robin is a priority in his plan. Under the microscope is Cormoran and Robin's relationship as they get closer whilst Robin's wedding plans continue to gather pace. Her fiance, Matthew, is clearly a ghastly secondary character just waiting to be written out. Cormoran's relationship with the Police remains a minefield that he has to negotiate delicately whilst taking out insurance.<br /><br />There is much mileage left in this ever improving and engaging series. It is tightly plotted to build the maximum level of tension and suspense with a fast paced narrative. I found it an entertaining, gripping and absorbing read. Cannot recommend it enough. Robert Galbraith is an assured and accomplished writer. I understand the BBC are going to film the series, I look forward to seeing what they make of this series! <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13737653871546170246" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6744204774867361242">Seeing the blurb for this book made me have this reaction:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437069251ra/15534855.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Reading this book made me have <i>this</i> reaction:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438653661ra/15739516.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>In some ways, this book was less intense than the impossibly disgusting, <i>Hannibal</i>-level grossness of <i>The Silkworm.</i> On the other hand, Galbraith's third benefits from taking a look into the dark personal histories of both Strike and Robin - specifically, the fact that they both have violent crime in their pasts - because it helps us, the readers, know a little more about why they're in this line</span>
  <span id="freeText6744204774867361242" style="display:none">Seeing the blurb for this book made me have this reaction:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437069251ra/15534855.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Reading this book made me have <i>this</i> reaction:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438653661ra/15739516.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In some ways, this book was less intense than the impossibly disgusting, <i>Hannibal</i>-level grossness of <i>The Silkworm.</i> On the other hand, Galbraith's third benefits from taking a look into the dark personal histories of both Strike and Robin - specifically, the fact that they both have violent crime in their pasts - because it helps us, the readers, know a little more about why they're in this line of work. And, in between all that, we're treated to another warped, bizarre world, mostly linked to Strike, with the worst side of rock and roll fandom involved. I might just find myself listening to a lot of Blue Oyster Cult after reading this book, just to get a better idea what this killer likes. It might just be the best serial-killer soundtrack since "Orinoco Flow" appeared in the 2011 <i>Dragon Tattoo</i> movie. Also, I might just find myself attempting to perfect my Cumbrian accent now - which, as it stands at the moment, is the unholy love child of Cockney and Scottish. Is it one of those accents that's impossible to fake if you're not a local? Maybe it is, but now I gotta try, don't I?<br><br>Now to sit back and wait for the fourth Strike book...it's gonna be another great one, I'm sure. This author cannot fail, I don't think. :)</span>
