<div id="review_1984788599" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1984788599" />
    <a title="Andrew Smith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5885760-andrew-smith"><img alt="Andrew Smith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605605555p2/5885760.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1984788599?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew Smith" href="/user/show/5885760-andrew-smith">Andrew Smith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/26877849-career-of-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1984788599" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5184905577819336261">A package delivered to a private investigator’s office in London contains the severed leg of a woman. Who sent this, and why? A note contained in the package that appears to be an extract from the lyrics of a song by the rock band the Blue Oyster Cult might offer a clue. The investigator, Cormoran Strike, is upset that his female partner was exposed to such a brutal discovery – for it was she the package was addressed to – but he thinks he can boil the list of perpetrators down to one of four me</span>
  <span id="freeText5184905577819336261" style="display:none">A package delivered to a private investigator’s office in London contains the severed leg of a woman. Who sent this, and why? A note contained in the package that appears to be an extract from the lyrics of a song by the rock band the Blue Oyster Cult might offer a clue. The investigator, Cormoran Strike, is upset that his female partner was exposed to such a brutal discovery – for it was she the package was addressed to – but he thinks he can boil the list of perpetrators down to one of four men. Strike’s observation that the leg is ‘not even my size’ heralds the discovery (for me) that he is missing a leg of his own. Interesting.<br /><br />I was quickly to discover that this was a very well crafted thriller indeed. After rejecting one of his four suspects as unlikely, Strike decides to leave that one to the police while he’ll try to track down the three dark men from his past who he feels are most capable of and incentivised to carry out this atrocious act. And the three men are grim characters indeed. Each is brought to life via the telling a back story and each is more deliciously appalling than the last. If the story had one of these fellows haunting the background of the piece it would have been interesting, but three… well that’s a feast!<br /><br />This is the third book the author has penned in this series, but as I haven’t read the first two I was somewhat concerned I’d suffer from that annoying tendency for there to be umpteen references I’d fail to grasp the significance of. I needn’t have worried. Galbraith (AKA J.K. Rowling, as I discovered to my utter surprise about half way through) deftly dealt with any relevant pre-story events by skilfully weaving the facts into the narrative. This is definitely a book that can be read as a stand-alone.<br /><br />I listened to the tale on audio, brilliantly read by British actor Robert Glenister. He brought each of the characters to life and skillfully delivered all the required accents. Even his Cornish accent sounded spot-on. Cormoran and his partner, Robin Ellacott, are interestingly complex and have plenty going on in their own lives to flesh out the action. There’s good chemistry between them and I’m definitely keen to meet up with them again.<br /><br />I found the pacing of the story to be just right and although the denouement didn’t provide the bombshell moment I’d been hoping for the whole thing was competently resolved come the end. I really felt at home with this tale. The tension was ever present and the hunt for the three grotesquely villainous bad guys was brilliantly handled. Who knew that the author of the Harry Potter books could also churn out top quality adult crime fiction too.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5184905577819336261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1429602408" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1429602408" />
    <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen"><img alt="Helene Jeppesen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528006866p2/21992464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1429602408?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helene Jeppesen" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen">Helene Jeppesen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316349932" href="/book/show/25735012-career-of-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1429602408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5159586306258714986">This book was amazing, and despite its size of 500 pages I read it in merely two days. Robert Galbraith, aka J. K. Rowling, seems to be the only author that can make me truly interested in crime stories, because normally they bore me as well as frustrate me (I can never seem to guess who the murderer is). <br/>Reading this third book in the Cormoran Strike series felt like coming home. I felt safe among some of my favourite characters, Robin and Strike, and because of them I read most of this book wi</span>
  <span id="freeText5159586306258714986" style="display:none">This book was amazing, and despite its size of 500 pages I read it in merely two days. Robert Galbraith, aka J. K. Rowling, seems to be the only author that can make me truly interested in crime stories, because normally they bore me as well as frustrate me (I can never seem to guess who the murderer is). <br />Reading this third book in the Cormoran Strike series felt like coming home. I felt safe among some of my favourite characters, Robin and Strike, and because of them I read most of this book with a smile on my face. Galbraith is truly amazing at writing characters, and I definitely think that the characters are what drives this story forward and makes me love it so much. <br />The murder case in itself interested me, but as is the case with the other two books as well, it was the relationship between Robin and Strike that kept me glued to the pages. I was able to follow the crime case and not be too bored, because Galbraith is really good at mingling it with the everyday lives of the characters. I'm a huge fan of this series, and I can't wait to get back to Robin and Strike in the fourth book - I already miss them! </span>
  <a data-text-id="5159586306258714986" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17452964045867857039">Career of Evil, the 3rd book in the Cormoran Strike series by J.K. Rowling is terrific and a favorite series of mine. This book did not disappoint. A little different in that Cormoran is not hired, but on a self-made journey with his partner, Robin Ellacott, to find a killer. <br/><br/>When a body part arrives for Robin at the office, the two of them set off to look at three men from Strike's past: his stepfather and two ex-soldiers, one a pedophile.   <span id="freeText17452964045867857039" style="display:none">Career of Evil, the 3rd book in the Cormoran Strike series by J.K. Rowling is terrific and a favorite series of mine. This book did not disappoint. A little different in that Cormoran is not hired, but on a self-made journey with his partner, Robin Ellacott, to find a killer. <br /><br />When a body part arrives for Robin at the office, the two of them set off to look at three men from Strike's past: his stepfather and two ex-soldiers, one a pedophile. Quite a gruesome trail is followed.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the intertwining of both of their personal and professional lives in Career of Evil. Robin's fiance, Matthew, made a nice triangle of intrigue and put into question whether their marriage would go forward.<br /><br />This was a very well written book with a delightful ending. I listened to the audiobook and again enjoyed the terrific British accent of the narrator. <br /><br />Can't wait for the next book. <br />A definite 5 out of 5 stars.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1397436141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1397436141" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1397436141?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780751562279" href="/book/show/24106033-career-of-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=awesome-audio">awesome-audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1397436141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2155761963488509101"><b>Sale Alert: Kindle Daily Deal May 24, 2020 <a href='https://www.amazon.com/dp/B0106E2CO6/ref=s9_acsd_hps_bw_c2_KCKDDGBs_17_t?pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&pf_rd_s=merchandised-search-2&pf_rd_r=AJC62CKTN5FEJTMBQDHM&pf_rd_t=101&pf_rd_p=2a2c4ce0-c45e-4331-840a-f13a10633114&pf_rd_i=11552285011' rel='nofollow noopener'>$4.99</a></b><br/><br/><b>3.5 Fish and Crisps Stars </b><br/><br/>I really do enjoy the gumshoe investigation stories that are The Cormoran Strike series. In this particular installment I enjoyed the actual case more than in the other two stories for a few reasons. One is that the nature of this case is more personal. <b>It all begins right off when Robin is sent a leg in the mail.</b> I don’t think it gets more personal than that and to our surprise Cormoran can think of about 4 people from hi</span>
  <span id="freeText2155761963488509101" style="display:none"><b>Sale Alert: Kindle Daily Deal May 24, 2020 <a href="https://www.amazon.com/dp/B0106E2CO6/ref=s9_acsd_hps_bw_c2_KCKDDGBs_17_t?pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&amp;pf_rd_s=merchandised-search-2&amp;pf_rd_r=AJC62CKTN5FEJTMBQDHM&amp;pf_rd_t=101&amp;pf_rd_p=2a2c4ce0-c45e-4331-840a-f13a10633114&amp;pf_rd_i=11552285011" rel="nofollow noopener">$4.99</a></b><br /><br /><b>3.5 Fish and Crisps Stars </b><br /><br />I really do enjoy the gumshoe investigation stories that are The Cormoran Strike series. In this particular installment I enjoyed the actual case more than in the other two stories for a few reasons. One is that the nature of this case is more personal. <b>It all begins right off when Robin is sent a leg in the mail.</b> I don’t think it gets more personal than that and to our surprise Cormoran can think of about 4 people from his past capable of such an act. <b>The other reason I liked this case a bit more is that we get some stuff from the PoV of the killer</b>. When done correctly I love being in the mind of the bad guy <i>it is a little tricky too much and it gets too uncomfortable, too little and there isn’t enough suspense added</i> but in this I think it was done really well. I like seeing his/her perspective and thought process it made everything just that much creepier. In this story specifically it added to the suspense and danger I felt specifically for Robin but also for Cormoran. <br /><br />I live for the interpersonal relationships in stories like these and while there were some developments it is still going a little slowly for my taste but I’m totally hooked and I’ll probably read the entire series just to see how it all works out. <b>I loved getting a bit into Robin’s backstory and why she left University</b>. I think her backstory explains a lot about the person she is today and why/how she and Matthew have been together for so long. I am also happy about a few of the developments between Strike and Robin. First and foremost they are good colleagues and work pretty well together most of the time. It is clear that each brings something to the business and Cormoran is seeing more and more what a benefit it is to have Robin in his life. But beyond that they are building a pretty strong friendship and even though there are some underlying feeling between them…not really addressed to each other they are at least starting to admit them to themselves.<br /><br />I’m a little disappointed in the Robin/Matthew dynamic and how it played out. But it fit both of their characters still very well and while I’m pulling for a Robin/Cormoran HEA eventually it seems like it is going to take a long time to get there if at all. There are some pretty big issues that I saw between Matthew and Robin in this installment that make it seem like either one of them has to change a lot or it is never going to work out. <b>Especially with it ending right where it did…</b>I really wonder how the story will open in the next book.<br /><br />I didn’t figure out who the killer really was until the last minute…like when the reveal was coming it all clicked into place. The reason that I’m only giving this a 3.5 have a little to do with pacing and a lot to do with Robin. Okay so I’m not sure if J.K. Rowling is brilliant in that she make you feel like the story is dragging a bit when they are having a lull in the case, because the characters are feeling the lull too or if it’s not on purpose at all. Either way there are times when everything just drags a bit. The other part is that Robin after the revelation of her past became a bit whiny. It was the first time that had happened and it really wasn’t becoming on her character. She never quite became TSTL (To Stupid To Live) but she did make some very rash decisions that led to some consequences in the story Robin wasn’t prepared to deal with.<br /><br />Overall I enjoy the writing and the characters so I’ll definitely continue on with the series. I however didn’t realize that there are around 8-10ish books planned in this series and so the interpersonal ARCs might take a lot longer to play out than I initially anticipated. I just hope I don’t get bored with that aspect of the series.<br /><br />One more time….Seriously THAT is where you ended it? Okay pretty brilliant but also, so soooo mean :P</span>
  <a data-text-id="2155761963488509101" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1422173834" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1422173834" />
    <a title="shakespeareandspice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2576681-shakespeareandspice"><img alt="shakespeareandspice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1497035907p2/2576681.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1422173834?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="shakespeareandspice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="shakespeareandspice" href="/user/show/2576681-shakespeareandspice">shakespeareandspice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316349932" href="/book/show/25735012-career-of-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1422173834" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15112010140118733398">Despite the fact that I love and adore Rowling for Harry Potter stories, I am disappointed to find, as an adult, how formulaic and simplistic her writing has become.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25735012.Career_of_Evil__Cormoran_Strike___3_' title='Career of Evil (Cormoran Strike, #3) by Robert Galbraith' rel='nofollow noopener'>Career of Evil</a> takes a darker turn to the first two novels in the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/108050-cormoran-strike' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cormoran Strike</a> series, and while I’m not entirely sure how I feel about this sudden change of atmosphere, the novel overall is a major disappointment. The likability of the series already hinges on the characters and the need to know what happens with them, but this b</span>
  <span id="freeText15112010140118733398" style="display:none">Despite the fact that I love and adore Rowling for Harry Potter stories, I am disappointed to find, as an adult, how formulaic and simplistic her writing has become.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25735012.Career_of_Evil__Cormoran_Strike___3_" title="Career of Evil (Cormoran Strike, #3) by Robert Galbraith" rel="nofollow noopener">Career of Evil</a> takes a darker turn to the first two novels in the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/108050-cormoran-strike" rel="nofollow noopener">Cormoran Strike</a> series, and while I’m not entirely sure how I feel about this sudden change of atmosphere, the novel overall is a major disappointment. The likability of the series already hinges on the characters and the need to know what happens with them, but this book is held up entirely by Robin and Strike’s drama. The mystery within the novel is actually more intense then the previous mysteries but it’s almost shoved into the corner amidst all the Strike-Robin drama.<br /><br />Rowling excels at characterizations, she is an absolute master at it, but it’s a bit problematic for me when a “mystery” novel is based more on the characters and their drama then the actual mystery. It’s a bit too much to expect from a reader. And honestly, the drama itself just festers and causes so much angst that this book had me actually clenching my teeth in frustration.<br /><br />Another aspect which seems typical of Rowling’s writing is info-dumping. While the novel is not at all difficult to read, and can be quite enjoyable at times, it’s tiresome when you are reading a 500 page novel and have to wait until the last 30-20% of it to understand everything that is going on. This is irritating, especially given that major portions of the novel just deal with Robin and Strike trying to avoid a conversation about their relationship.<br /><br />Strike is a character I’ve never been able to get truly attached to, but that was not much of a concern seeing as how these are ultimately mystery novels and it doesn’t matter if I love him or not because he’s just a detective and all I cared about was that he did his job. Robin, however, is absolutely infuriating. I used to be able to sympathize with her but her character is so childish, filled with so much teenage anxiety that I couldn’t stand her halfway into the book. I had a hard time picturing her as an adult by the end, all I kept seeing was a 15 year old girl who had no clue what life was about. I felt bad for her, but ultimately just couldn’t care enough. It’s fairly easy for me to get attached to female characters but as this novel progressed, I felt myself pulling away from her.<br /><br />Generally, I would say this novel would work better as TV series (since those allow for more stereotypical drama). As a <i>mystery</i> novel, this book is a disaster.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15112010140118733398" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer7269342136359402283">I always look forward to picking up a book by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1077326.J_K__Rowling' title='J.K. Rowling' rel='nofollow noopener'>J.K. Rowling</a>. From <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3.Harry_Potter_and_the_Sorcerer_s_Stone__Harry_Potter___1_' title='Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone (Harry Potter, #1) by J.K. Rowling' rel='nofollow noopener'>Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone</a> through to this current novel she has never put a foot wrong and I firmly believe she could write successfully in any genre. A truly talented author.<br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25735012.Career_of_Evil__Cormoran_Strike___3_' title='Career of Evil (Cormoran Strike, #3) by Robert Galbraith' rel='nofollow noopener'>Career of Evil</a> is the third in a series which hopefully will be a long one! The two main characters, Stryke and Robin, are wonderful and the trials and tribulations of their relationship are handled beautifully, to the point where this reader at le</span>
  <span id="freeText7269342136359402283" style="display:none">I always look forward to picking up a book by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1077326.J_K__Rowling" title="J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">J.K. Rowling</a>. From <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3.Harry_Potter_and_the_Sorcerer_s_Stone__Harry_Potter___1_" title="Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone (Harry Potter, #1) by J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone</a> through to this current novel she has never put a foot wrong and I firmly believe she could write successfully in any genre. A truly talented author.<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25735012.Career_of_Evil__Cormoran_Strike___3_" title="Career of Evil (Cormoran Strike, #3) by Robert Galbraith" rel="nofollow noopener">Career of Evil</a> is the third in a series which hopefully will be a long one! The two main characters, Stryke and Robin, are wonderful and the trials and tribulations of their relationship are handled beautifully, to the point where this reader at least continues to think about them long after the book is finished! Some new characters pop up too and the mystery is thrilling, well paced and cleverly written. An easy five stars and I am not at all surprised there is to be a TV show. Looking forward to that and also the next book.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1492634799" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1492634799" />
    <a title="Barbara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2172096-barbara"><img alt="Barbara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598060221p2/2172096.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1492634799?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara" href="/user/show/2172096-barbara">Barbara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316349932" href="/book/show/25735012-career-of-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2172096-barbara?shelf=2016-challenge">2016-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2172096-barbara?shelf=wom-2015-challenge">wom-2015-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1492634799" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4678003151804114847"><br/><b> 3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>This is the third book in Robert Galbraith's (aka J.K. Rowling) series about grizzled private detective Cormoran Strike, a veteran of the war in Afghanistan who lost his leg during the hostilities, and his pretty, strawberry blonde partner Robin Ellacott.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578329530i/28724900.jpg' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>As the story opens Strike and Robin are working on a couple of cases and getting on with their private lives: Strike is dating beautiful (almost) divorcée Elin.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578329530i/28724901.jpg' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>And Robin is planning her wedding to Matthew - a handsome but insensitive g</span>
  <span id="freeText4678003151804114847" style="display:none"><br><b> 3.5 stars</b><br><br>This is the third book in Robert Galbraith's (aka J.K. Rowling) series about grizzled private detective Cormoran Strike, a veteran of the war in Afghanistan who lost his leg during the hostilities, and his pretty, strawberry blonde partner Robin Ellacott.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578329530i/28724900.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As the story opens Strike and Robin are working on a couple of cases and getting on with their private lives: Strike is dating beautiful (almost) divorcée Elin.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578329530i/28724901.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And Robin is planning her wedding to Matthew - a handsome but insensitive guy who resents Robin's job and her friendship with Strike. (As before, most readers probably wonder how Robin can continue her relationship with this irritating guy.)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578329530i/28724902.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Robin receives a package at the Detective Agency and - thinking it's some wedding doodads - opens it to find the severed right leg of a young woman.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578329530i/28724903.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Not only is this horrifying but it seems to be sending a message because Strike is missing his right leg. Strike concludes that the package was most likely sent by one of three men who hate him:<br><br>Jeff Whittaker, Strike's former stepfather - a loutish, abusive, would-be rock star that Strike believes murdered his mother.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578329530i/28724904.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Donald Laing, a vicious man who once bit Strike's face during an Army boxing match. Later, when Strike was in the Military Police, he arrested Laing for horrific wife abuse and helped imprison him for 16 years.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578329530i/28724905.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Noel Brockbank, a serial pedophile who escaped prison because Strike struck him during an arrest. Brockbank blames Strike for his brain injury and epileptic fits.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578329530i/28724906.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Strike reports his suspicions of the three men to the police but they decide to concentrate on other leads, in part because they resent Strike - who became famous after solving a couple of high-profile cases that eluded the cops. So Strike and Robin take it upon themselves to track down the three suspects while continuing to work their ongoing cases.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578329530i/28724907.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Meanwhile, the killer goes on with his murderous spree. Parts of the story are narrated by the perp, who graphically describes how he abducts and kills young women. The psychopath seethes with jealousy and hatred for Strike and is determined to ruin his life, partly through targeting Robin. Thus, the killer sends another body part to Strike's partner.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578329530i/28724908.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Though it's clear the killer has Robin in his sights, she's determined to be a good detective and an asset to the agency. Thus, Robin refuses to take proper precautions and finds herself in some dangerous situations.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578329530i/28724910.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For me, this was hard to buy into. If I knew a depraved serial killer was following me around I'd for sure take cover - preferably in a bomb shelter.<br><br>Strike and Robin's pursuit of the killer takes them around London and to other parts of Great Britain as they follow leads, question people, investigate dwellings, and so on. During their inquiries the detectives come across a group of people that have 'body integrity disorder', a mental illness that creates an obsession to have one or more limbs amputated. This is especially infuriating to Strike, whose life is greatly hampered by the absence of a leg.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578329530i/28724909._SX540_.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As all this is going on, Strike and Robin struggle with a mutual attraction that both seem reluctant to acknowledge.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578329530i/28724912.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Matthew also inadvertently reveals a secret that throws a spanner into his and Robin's upcoming marriage plans. In addition, the story reveals incidents that profoundly affected Robin and Strike in their pasts, which have continuing repercussions. It will be interesting to see how this plays out in future books.<br><br>After a good deal of drama and danger, Strike gets a 'eureka moment' that helps him solve the case. For me, this part didn't ring true and I felt unsatisfied with the story's climax. Other than that though, I enjoyed the book and recommend it to mystery fans. <br><br>You can follow my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot.com/">http://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4678003151804114847" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1419290183?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kirsty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kirsty" href="/user/show/76596-kirsty">Kirsty</a>
      </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6442116651316012513">JK Rowling continues to astonish me. First, of course, with her Harry Potter books she created a world to which I return over and over as a delighted and bedazzled reader. Her accomplishment with that series marks her as a once-in-a-generation storyteller.<br/><br/>But she also writes adult mystery/crime novels under the pseudonym of Robert Galbraith. And they are very, very good, especially this one, her third that follows the adventures of private detective Cormoran Strike. <br/><br/>I'm astonished at and gratefu</span>
  <span id="freeText6442116651316012513" style="display:none">JK Rowling continues to astonish me. First, of course, with her Harry Potter books she created a world to which I return over and over as a delighted and bedazzled reader. Her accomplishment with that series marks her as a once-in-a-generation storyteller.<br /><br />But she also writes adult mystery/crime novels under the pseudonym of Robert Galbraith. And they are very, very good, especially this one, her third that follows the adventures of private detective Cormoran Strike. <br /><br />I'm astonished at and grateful for her talent, determination, and willingness to keep writing great books. Highly recommended, with the caveat that a few scenes are extremely violent.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1727048236?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2337007-brenda?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2337007-brenda?shelf=own-read">own-read</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1727048236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16353389783180653979">Book #3 in the Cormoran Strike series by Robert Galbraith (aka JK Rowling) is another great episode which features Strike and his able assistant Robin Ellacott. It was when Robin received a strangely shaped package by courier – which she thought would be wedding paraphernalia for her upcoming nuptials with fiancé Matthew – and discovered a woman’s leg, that the business began to falter, and both Robin’s and Strike’s lives changed. <br/><br/>As Robin and Strike focused on finding the perpetrator, the polic</span>
  <span id="freeText16353389783180653979" style="display:none">Book #3 in the Cormoran Strike series by Robert Galbraith (aka JK Rowling) is another great episode which features Strike and his able assistant Robin Ellacott. It was when Robin received a strangely shaped package by courier – which she thought would be wedding paraphernalia for her upcoming nuptials with fiancé Matthew – and discovered a woman’s leg, that the business began to falter, and both Robin’s and Strike’s lives changed. <br /><br />As Robin and Strike focused on finding the perpetrator, the police felt they had little to go on. Frustration marred their daily lives, while danger hovered on the periphery with a psychopath determined to do his utmost. And as more victims were found, the web tightened. Would Strike have success in his endeavours to catch the person responsible?<br /><br />Enjoyable – a little too long at almost 500 pages – but highly recommended.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16353389783180653979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1173707034" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1173707034" />
    <a title="Ashley Marie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29787548-ashley-marie"><img alt="Ashley Marie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471208025p2/29787548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1173707034?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Marie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Marie " href="/user/show/29787548-ashley-marie">Ashley Marie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/26877849-career-of-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29787548-ashley-marie?shelf=wtf-did-i-just-read">wtf-did-i-just-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29787548-ashley-marie?shelf=killer-thriller-night">killer-thriller-night</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1173707034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1182235052550988866">I like to think of myself as a critical reader. As such, I'm mad at myself that it took me an <a href='https://www.vice.com/en_us/article/pkeynz/jk-rowlings-transphobia-wasnt-hard-to-find-she-wrote-a-book-about-it' rel='nofollow noopener'>article</a> with in-text references to point out the racism and transphobia in this series. Rating adjusted, and original review under the spoiler tags.<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[3.5 stars, rounded up to 4 because Jo's characterizations are brilliant.<br/><br/>I feel like I don't know where to start! This felt really consistent with the first two books (that is, if you liked them, you'll probably like this one too) and I lovelov</span></span>
  <span id="freeText1182235052550988866" style="display:none">I like to think of myself as a critical reader. As such, I'm mad at myself that it took me an <a href="https://www.vice.com/en_us/article/pkeynz/jk-rowlings-transphobia-wasnt-hard-to-find-she-wrote-a-book-about-it" rel="nofollow noopener">article</a> with in-text references to point out the racism and transphobia in this series. Rating adjusted, and original review under the spoiler tags.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[3.5 stars, rounded up to 4 because Jo's characterizations are brilliant.<br /><br />I feel like I don't know where to start! This felt really consistent with the first two books (that is, if you liked them, you'll probably like this one too) and I lovelovelove Robin. Also, thanks to Kaora, I'll now and forever picture Strike as Liev Schreiber. Thanks ;) My original mental image of Brian d'Arcy James got scrapped because Liev is just too perfect. ANYWAY. <br /><br />The Robin/Strike dynamic is wonderful and they make such a good team -- I kind of-sort of ship them but at the same time not really because I don't want a relationship to screw up what they've got going on. The case this time was a lot of surveillance of three different guys, which dragged a bit because all they're doing is splitting up and sitting there keeping tabs on whether anything weird happens or not. Matthew certainly did his part to keep things interesting, the twit. Overdramatic, more like. He's beyond infuriating and I honestly think Jo likes him that way :P Alas, they can't all be likeable, can they? I'm very irked by their whole saga, because I used to be in a relationship like that where he was extremely insecure about the people I worked with and so on. It didn't get better and that ended at least five years ago now. <br /><br />I LOVED Shanker's character, he was a brilliant addition to the cast and I really hope he pops up again. You could really feel Robin's stress mounting throughout the book, from page one to the end and I think this was really her time to shine as a character. Jo has said in interviews that Robin Ellacott is her favorite of all her characters she's ever written, and we see so much of the story through Robin's eyes that I can't ignore her on that point. <br /><br />Now I'm dying to go back and reread all three books because I've screwed up on figuring out the culprit all three times, damn it!<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="1182235052550988866" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1678301848" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1678301848" />
    <a title="Warda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30036082-warda"><img alt="Warda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593385153p2/30036082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1678301848?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780751563597" href="/book/show/27845654-career-of-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1678301848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4395543752787523839">OH MY WORD! ROWLING, GIMME THE NEXT BOOK!!!!<br/><br/>Epic cliffhanger. Cruel cliffhanger! This book was everything!!!! *major heart eyes* <br/><br/>This instalment was definitely my favourite out of three. The character development was excellent. We explored and delved a lot more deeper into the pasts of both Strike and Robin, which was quite dark, but you can't help but love these two! Individually, they're amazing. Together, they would be even more amazing. Make it happen, Rowling!<br/><br/>The plot was slightly creepy an</span>
  <span id="freeText4395543752787523839" style="display:none">OH MY WORD! ROWLING, GIMME THE NEXT BOOK!!!!<br /><br />Epic cliffhanger. Cruel cliffhanger! This book was everything!!!! *major heart eyes* <br /><br />This instalment was definitely my favourite out of three. The character development was excellent. We explored and delved a lot more deeper into the pasts of both Strike and Robin, which was quite dark, but you can't help but love these two! Individually, they're amazing. Together, they would be even more amazing. Make it happen, Rowling!<br /><br />The plot was slightly creepy and a lot more gory than the others and I loved that! I also loved that we got the added POV of the antagonist. The build-up towards the end was done extremely well. I was flippin anxious!!! Then the last 100 pages happened and I have no words. Especially that last, last paragraph. WHAT?!<br /><br />The only minor complaint I have is that I don't think the mystery was wrapped up as cohesively as I would've liked (or maybe I was reading so fast at this point, I ended up missing some things) but I'm hoping it'll continue on in the next book. <br /><br />Can we get a release date already?! <br /><br />No doubt this book is going to be playing on my mind for a while. I freakin adored to pieces. I'm already looking forward to rereading all of them. <br /><br />P.S. Matthew is a bitch. <br />P.P.S. He needs to get ditched ASAP!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4395543752787523839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZZlNIh/fXQcywV8ExzoBYY1kFcc3fn46/4g6laMVihMcZLu+cFW1HAt+K4P9+0Ks0+hFYcpEXQRPGltdlmUaGw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BKefC+PJNJLs+OwXvb0unhSYcHT0gb2NObSjwPvAixd9WmmXjEPcidVHmJCHfG1TShQg0gm7nrOJJsIIzrAbHw==')})
  }

Robert Galbraith’s latest novel is the third installment in the popular Cormoran Strike detective series. Penned by Harry Potter author J.K. The insight to their personal lives provides the reader with a better understanding of their motivations all the while adding to the suspense in the plot.  Private detective Cormoran Strike has found recent fame in the press after solving two murder investigations with the help of his assistant, Robin Ellacott. The two of them have just slipped back into a more typical work routine when Robin receives a package in the mail that contains the severed leg of a woman. Strike is haunted by the memories of men he has crossed paths with in the past, men who have reason to seek vengeance upon him. He offers their names up to the police officers working the case, but when it appears they are not taking him seriously, Strike and Robin decide to take the investigation into their own hands.           $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});

      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_16243').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_16243').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_16243').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/383606.Robert_Galbraith">About Robert Galbraith</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/383606.Robert_Galbraith"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_111x148-e08b4682eea7088f8cdfd67c131d51cd.png);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9517594061840859444"><i>This is a pseudonym for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1077326.J_K_Rowling' rel='nofollow noopener'> J.K. Rowling</a>, the author of the Harry Potter series and </i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13497818-the-casual-vacancy' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Casual Vacancy,</a><i> a novel for adults.</i><br/><br/><i>
  <b>NOTE: There is more than one author with this name on Goodreads.</b>
</i><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7171901.Robert_Galbraith' rel='nofollow noopener'>Robert Galbraith - Marine Biologist</a><br/><br/>Rowling was born to Anne Rowling (née Volant) and Peter James Rowling, a Rolls-Royce aircraft engineer, on 31 July 1965 in Yate, Gloucestershire, England, 10 miles (16 km) north</span>
  <span id="freeText9517594061840859444" style="display:none"><i>This is a pseudonym for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1077326.J_K_Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener"> J.K. Rowling</a>, the author of the Harry Potter series and </i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13497818-the-casual-vacancy" rel="nofollow noopener">The Casual Vacancy,</a><i> a novel for adults.</i><br /><br /><i>
  <b>NOTE: There is more than one author with this name on Goodreads.</b>
</i><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7171901.Robert_Galbraith" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Galbraith - Marine Biologist</a><br /><br />Rowling was born to Anne Rowling (née Volant) and Peter James Rowling, a Rolls-Royce aircraft engineer, on 31 July 1965 in Yate, Gloucestershire, England, 10 miles (16 km) northeast of Bristol. Her mother Anne was half-French and half-Scottish. Her parents first met on a train departing from King's Cross Station bound for Arbroath in 1964. They married on 14 March 1965. Her mother's maternal grandfather, Dugald Campbell, was born in Lamlash on the Isle of Arran. Her mother's paternal grandfather, Louis Volant, was awarded the Croix de Guerre for exceptional bravery in defending the village of Courcelles-le-Comte during the First World War.<br /><br />Rowling's sister Dianne was born at their home when Rowling was 23 months old. The family moved to the nearby village Winterbourne when Rowling was four. She attended St Michael's Primary School, a school founded by abolitionist William Wilberforce and education reformer Hannah More. Her headmaster at St Michael's, Alfred Dunn, has been suggested as the inspiration for the Harry Potter headmaster Albus Dumbledore.<br /><br />As a child, Rowling often wrote fantasy stories, which she would usually then read to her sister. She recalls that: "I can still remember me telling her a story in which she fell down a rabbit hole and was fed strawberries by the rabbit family inside it. Certainly the first story I ever wrote down (when I was five or six) was about a rabbit called Rabbit. He got the measles and was visited by his friends, including a giant bee called Miss Bee." At the age of nine, Rowling moved to Church Cottage in the Gloucestershire village of Tutshill, close to Chepstow, Wales. When she was a young teenager, her great aunt, who Rowling said "taught classics and approved of a thirst for knowledge, even of a questionable kind," gave her a very old copy of Jessica Mitford's autobiography, Hons and Rebels. Mitford became Rowling's heroine, and Rowling subsequently read all of her books.<br /><br />Rowling has said of her teenage years, in an interview with <i>The New Yorker,</i> "I wasn’t particularly happy. I think it’s a dreadful time of life." She had a difficult homelife; her mother was ill and she had a difficult relationship with her father (she is no longer on speaking terms with him). She attended secondary school at Wyedean School and College, where her mother had worked as a technician in the science department. Rowling said of her adolescence, "Hermione [a bookish, know-it-all Harry Potter character] is loosely based on me. She's a caricature of me when I was eleven, which I'm not particularly proud of." Steve Eddy, who taught Rowling English when she first arrived, remembers her as "not exceptional" but "one of a group of girls who were bright, and quite good at English." Sean Harris, her best friend in the Upper Sixth owned a turquoise Ford Anglia, which she says inspired the one in her books.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9517594061840859444" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
